 It’s a brute game 
↳ Why does it matter? 
AI is becoming a brute force game. A recent survey in Nature shows that scientists 
are struggling to keep up with industry due to lack of infrastructure, computing 
power, energy, and funding. Yet, AI has immense potential. Software engineers have 
seen productivity double in just a few months using AI tools like co-pilots, reducing 
development time by 50%. However, the high costs associated with AI mean most of 
the world lacks the resources to compete. This raises a big question: Can AI be an 
equalizer, or will it amplify existing differences? 
↳ My thoughts on it 
It’s both. AI could unlock productivity gains that help those at the bottom of the 
pyramid, but that’s a tricky proposition. The survey focused on advanced economies; 
if their universities are behind industry, imagine the gap elsewhere. I see so much 
potential in AI—I can’t imagine life without it now. But how can we use it to improve 
the world? Strategically, countries have limited room to maneuver due to high 
resource demands—think Latam, Africa, Southeast Asia... Most lack the governance 
and strategic capabilities to make focused decisions. That’s worrisome. As always, 
tech is not the constraint.

 Dangerous fields 
↳ Why does it matter? 
In short: because the risk of escalation. On November 21, Russia used a new type of 
mid-range balistic hypersonic MIRV missile to attack Ukraine. Just days before, the 
United States authorized Ukraine to use American missiles to reach targets inside 
Russia. Recent reports suggest Russia may (or is suggesting it can) deploy these 
new defense technologies to the Asia-Pacific  region. Tensions are increasing, raising 
questions about how to de-escalate the situation and end the conflict.  
↳ My thoughts on it

burst in 2021 with the Russian invasion. Increasingly, each side pushes the other into 
more dangerous territory. What will be the outcome if this dynamic is continued? 
Some in the West believe (I don’t have intel and I am not qualified   to make an 
assessment) that Russia will exhaust its technological, financial, political, and 
military resources, but that may not be a safe bet for all of us in this planet. It would 
be wiser if we could avoid a nuclear conflict.  Watch closely the next moves, from all 
sides.

 Reality imposes itself 
↳ Why does it matter? 
For the first time, the African Union (AU) participated as a full member at the G20 
meeting in Rio de Janeiro last week. Africa is the fastest-growing continent, 
expected to exceed 4 billion people by the end of the century. It has immense 
potential—imagine the market—and significant   challenges. Including Africa in global 
conversations is crucial. Ignoring it could lead to serious consequences—imagine 
the turmoil if hundreds of millions migrate to Europe in search of something very 
basic: opportunities. However, the AU's participation was barely noticed in 
mainstream media. Aren’t we missing something here? Whatever it is, at some point, 
reality imposes itself—the scale of Africa's challenges and opportunities can no 
longer be overlooked. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
While much of the Western media focused on President Xi Jinping's visit to Latin 
America, including the opening of a new port in Peru, the inclusion of the African 
Union in the G20 could signify a fundamental change. China's economic influence in 
Latin America is growing. However, by the end of the century, China's population is 
projected to halve compared to today’s level, while Africa's will be 5–6 times larger 
than that of China. Africa holds immense potential—with abundant natural resources 
and a young, dynamic population—and even Venture Capital, still limited and new, is 
growing there despite the ‘dry markets’ in most of the globe. A final question: with 
the African Union's addition, shouldn’t the Forum now be called the G21? Something 
to think about.

 Voltswagen may be in the horizon

----------------Page (225) Break----------------

 Be ready, nuclear fusion is coming 
↳ Why does it matter? 
Nuclear energy is crucial for decarbonization, especially as power consumption 
surges due to the rise of AI and electrification,  such as electric vehicles. It offers 
reliable, clean baseline power and resilience to geopolitical shifts. Advancements in 
nuclear technology are introducing innovations beyond traditional large fission 
reactors, including small modular reactors and the progressing promise of fusion 
energy. In 2022, experiments in the U.S. and U.K. achieved net energy gain from 
fusion, and nuclear fusion startups are entering the market. Realizing fusion's 
potential could lead to unprecedented energy abundance, disrupting energy markets 
and causing a massive global shift. However, fusion has been a moving target, and 
new models are needed to accelerate its market integration. 
----------------Page (226) Break----------------
↳ My thoughts on it 
Nuclear fusion has been a moving target. The largest project in the world, ITER in 
France, involves many nations, including Russia. It's faced significant   budget 
overruns. Now, a profusion of startups are joining the race, and there's healthy 
competition between big government projects like ITER and private startups. 
Different technologies are vying for success: tokamaks vs. laser fusion. It's an 
exciting moment. Some say fusion could reach the market in 10 years, as colleagues 
from Longview Fusion. But new solutions and initiatives are still needed to 
accelerate fusion technology into the market, and we should expect more and more 
news about it in the years to come. Get ready—the world may be transformed in our 
lifetime. 
↳ Read more here  
https://bit.ly/3Ocf10a

costs. The port is already the largest in the region, and this development occurs 
----------------Page (227) Break----------------

↳ My thoughts on it

(Bolivia). Historically, Brazil and Spanish-speaking nations in Latin America have 
looked north to Europe, the U.S., and China, but not to others in the region. Building 
infrastructure is crucial at both regional and national levels—there are significant   
infrastructure and investment gaps across the region. Countries need capital to 
invest and access to global markets. This new port could reduce shipping times by 
ten days between China and Brazil (when land connections are fully built), benefiting  
not just Brazil but also Peru, Bolivia, Chile, Argentina, and Colombia. From a Latin

 BRICS is slated to add a new letter 
↳ Why does it matter? 
Turkey’s bid to join BRICS signals ongoing geostrategic shifts in the world. Turkey’s 
play, especially in energy and its balancing act between Russia and the West, 
highlights the complex dynamics that BRICS faces. As the group expands, managing 
diverse interests becomes harder and the need for some kind of structure becomes 
more evident. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
BRICS is an acronym in search of a soul. China drove much of the economic growth 
in the group since it became known as such, while others lag. The common threads 
are the search for new capital and growth sources and a desire to advance 
relationships and frameworks that are not dominated or mediated by Western 
----------------Page (253) Break----------------
Europe and the US. The big question is: if the so-called BRICS countries could 
redesign the global system, how different would it look from Bretton Woods?

 AI regulation gains momentum  
↳ Why does it matter? 
----------------Page (254) Break----------------
California's economy is driven by technology. The state legislature just passed 
legislation to regulate AI. Bill SB-1047, supported by Elon Musk to the surprise of 
some, mandates companies to implement a controversial "kill switch.” This is 
pioneering legislation of this type and is also part of an emerging global issue. 
Expect more AI regulations worldwide. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
Balancing regulation and innovation is tough, especially in fast-moving tech areas. 
Governor Newsom will need to decide whether to sign the bill into law or not. For an 
economy driven by tech and digital, this is critical. Governments globally will soon 
face similar decisions. Speed matters and societies aren't prepared to deal with 
digital tech. From a policy perspective, it is essential to build a body of knowledge on 
the matter, distill lessons, and structure best practices.

 A drone may be coming for you 
↳ Why does it matter? 
Drones are now key in warfare, as seen in Russia, Ukraine, and the Middle East. Their 
use is spreading globally, even to non-state actors. This signals the rise of 
asymmetric warfare, which is becoming the norm. It also highlights the challenges 
that come with new technologies and their democratization. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
----------------Page (255) Break----------------
Citizens dodging drones feels like sci-fi,  but it's real and already happening. Today, 
most drones are piloted remotely (like the FPVs being used by the Ukrainian military), 
but autonomous AI-powered drones are inevitable. The risk isn't just military 
use—soon, anyone could have this power, including organized crime, terrorists, and 
rogue individuals. Are law enforcement agencies ready?

https://bit.ly/3Xc23nm

 Capital shifts 
↳ Why does it matter? 
Capital is concentrated in advanced economies. However, shifts are happening. 
China’s foreign investment grew over 5,700% from 2002 to 2022, and the UAE’s grew 
5,500%, while the outflow   of EU’s FDI was reduced by 48%. For comparison: 
American FDI grew 176%, and the world’s grew 200%. These emerging capital hubs 
are increasingly connecting their financial markets. This is being coupled with the 
digitalization of currencies and the expansion of cross-border payment systems. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
Capital available for emerging nations is shifting hands. Countries like the UAE and 
China bring new rules for engagement. We'll see new financial tools emerging from 
these new global capital hubs and more connections between their markets. 
Understanding the dynamics and being capable of connecting with new sources of 
capital is key to seizing opportunities in a changing world, for businesses and 
emerging countries. This challenges the influence of advanced economies in the 
Global South, and tensions may arise. 
----------------Page (256) Break----------------

Welcome to another edition of the Weekly Snapshot! Let’s dive in, and don’t forget to

 Atoms matter in geopolitics and business 
↳ Why does it matter? 
Global demand for critical minerals is surging (e.g.: the demand for Lithium grew 
30% in 2023, Cobalt ~10%), with production concentrated in a few areas. China, 
anticipating this trend, has better coordinated its efforts, dominating production and 
expanding access in Africa. These minerals are vital for manufacturing computer 
chips, electronics, clean tech, and advanced materials. This move will increase 
tensions and can accelerate moves. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
----------------Page (257) Break----------------
We’re likely to see more U.S.-China curbs, with the U.S. targeting high-tech and China 
focusing on minerals. It is a lose-lose game, and a dangerous one. This dynamics 
will drive more investment in mineral and tech research in the West. New methods 
for locating, harvesting, and processing minerals are needed, along with accelerated 
development of synthetic minerals and urban mining. This trend also reinforces 
nationalization and ‘friend shoring’ efforts-in mineral production, manufacturing, and 
across supply chains. 
↳ Read more here  
https://bit.ly/4dEhhIF 
https://bit.ly/3AF16MK 
 AR/VR still has to surpass the ‘deceptive’ phase 
↳ Why does it matter? 
Facebook acquired Oculus in March 2014. From 2020 to 2024, its metaverse division 
reportedly lost $42 billion. Market forecasts for AR, VR, and the metaverse have 
fallen short, with products like Meta's Quest and Apple's Vision Pro underperforming. 
The products are expensive, are not selling as expected and, a rarely disclosed 
statistics, 40% of users suffer nausea when wearing VR googles. Is this the end? No, 
it's a big opportunity. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
The AR/VR market in 2024 is valued at about $30 billion, with an estimated 35% 
annual growth until the decade's end. Despite this, consumer adoption is lagging. 
We're in the "deception phase," where early expectations haven't been met, but this 
signals opportunities for new technologies and producers. A breakthrough AR/VR 
technology, offering experiences with devices much like everyday glasses (I’ve seen 
----------------Page (258) Break----------------
and handled a proof of concept—get in contact in you want to know where), is on the 
horizon. It's just a matter of time. The key question is who will invest to accelerate 
development and build the necessary business structure to gain the market. 
↳ Read more here  
https://bit.ly/473DTQl 
https://bit.ly/4762nZd 
https://bit.ly/4cIJa14 
 From the biotech front: a first for LatAm 
↳ Why does it matter? 
Zoonotic virus jumps are on the rise, making pandemics and epidemics more 
frequent. There are 51 BSL-4 labs in operation worldwide. Latin America, with 670 
million people, has lacked a high-security biolab—until now. Brazil is leading with the 
first such facility in the region. This is significant   for health, technological, and 
management advancements in the country and Latin America. It's also a world first, 
combining a synchrotron light source with a high-security biolab. This feat displays 
ambition, addresses a real need, and will create opportunities to advance critical 
capabilities. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
CNPEM is a complex of Brazilian national labs, government-funded but managed by 
a non-profit.  It embodies much-needed institutional innovation in Brazil, Latin 
America, and the emerging world at large. CNPEM's model is the closest alignment 
within Brazilian legal constraints to the U.S. national labs model. The new BSL-4 lab 
will bring challenges, particularly in funding, technical integration with the light 
----------------Page (259) Break----------------
source, and human resources. Developing specialized skills and implementing the 
processes needed for the secure operation of the new lab will be crucial and cannot 
be neglected. Overcoming these challenges can create significant   opportunities and 
even inspire other emerging nations—yes, we can. But institutional improvement is 
essential to turning challenges into opportunities. 
↳ Read more here  
https://bit.ly/3ADAhZr 
https://bit.ly/3XkeEWW 
https://bit.ly/3Mm2TJ9

 German automakers bet on wheel hub motors 
↳ Why does it matter? 
----------------Page (260) Break----------------
German carmakers are losing ground in China and globally. What could potentially 
change the game? A tech breakthrough. Porsche introduced in-wheel drive to the 
world in 1900, but the project was eventually abandoned. Hyundai announced its on 
wheel motor in Nov 2023. Now, a German startup claims to have developed a version 
that is 20% more efficient than standard EVs, and BMW is testing it. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
Sales of EVs and hybrids in China now account for 50% of the total market. It is 
increasingly difficult  for foreign automakers to penetrate the Chinese market. 
Whether ‘hub motors’ can change the game remains to be seen. However, this new 
technology could further lower EV prices and reduce total ownership costs, 
potentially accelerating market penetration globally.

 UK launches into space 
↳ Why does it matter? 
The UK has been somewhat reserved in space exploration, with the UK Space 
Agency established only in 2010. However, space has become a major frontier, and 
interest in space technologies is growing globally, including for defense and warfare. 
On-Earth military operations increasingly depend on space capabilities. The launch 
of Tyche, a military Earth-imaging satellite, marks a significant   first for the UK. 
----------------Page (261) Break----------------
↳ My thoughts on it 
Tyche has a 90 cm resolution, while US and Chinese defense satellites achieve 10 
cm or higher. Expect more military activity in space and a revisitation of the 
International Outer Space Treaty and space law in general. While the UK strives to 
develop military space capabilities, its new space economy thrives, attracting more 
private investment in space than any country outside the US since 2015. Strong 
science capabilities could give the UK an edge. 
↳ Read more here  
https://bit.ly/3ADKrJe 
https://bit.ly/4cEMEBO

 A breakthrough in protein design can enable future biobots 
↳ Why does it matter? 
Having the capacity to turn proteins "on" and "off" allows us to send instructions and 
perform logic operations (like "if") within biological structures. This is the first step 
toward creating "switchable" higher-order nanomaterials and, eventually, 
components such as pumps, conveyors, walkers, and even fully structured 
bio-machines and biobots. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
We are still in the early days of biodesign, and bio machines remain largely 
conceptual, but the promise and potential are immense. This fundamental 
development will accelerate research in the field and likely shorten the time needed 
----------------Page (262) Break----------------
to achieve functional "switchable" biomaterials and bio machines. We've never been 
this close, and the momentum is now building. 
↳ Read more here  
https://bit.ly/3XcXaM8

 A robot plays ping-pong during the Olympics season 
↳ Why does it matter? 
Sports are complex endeavors from a computational and modeling perspective. This 
feat by Deep Mind marks the first time a robot has played a sport with humans in a 
competitive way. Importantly, it was fun for the humans involved. Deep Mind used an 
innovative approach to train the AI algorithms that control the robot, and this new 
method can be applied in other contexts, such as manufacturing or piloting. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
The promise of human-like robots has not yet been realized, but we are getting 
closer. This case may be remembered as a turning point in the relationship between 
humans, robots, and sports. Have you seen the objective of the RoboCup? If not, 
follow the link to check it out. In the manufacturing world, Figure 2 robots have been 
deployed at a BMW factory in the US—also take a look at what UBTECH and Mentee 
Robotics are doing. We should expect things to accelerate.

 The cybercrime treaty moved forward in the UN 
↳ Why does it matter? 
Cybercrime is rising at a rate of 15% per year. The global cost of cybercrime is 
expected to double by 2029, reaching $16 trillion. Most cybercrimes occur across 
borders, requiring countries to coordinate their actions. It's encouraging that even in 
a period of growing global tensions, the world finds space for some collaboration. 
↳ My thoughts on it 
Russia introduced the original draft for the cybercrime treaty, which was 
unanimously approved after three years of negotiations. Big tech and privacy civil 
society groups oppose the treaty, highlighting ongoing tensions between 
governments and tech companies. The outcomes remain to be seen. Between 
“surveillance state” and “big tech dominance,” the world faces challenges. Our 
institutions are not fit for the digital world.

 China finds signals of water in the Moon 
----------------Page (267) Break----------------
↳ Why does it matter?

competition in space exploration and technology.

 The AI race becomes physical 
↳ Why does it matter? 
AI models are progressing, but hardware is now also a major frontier for AI 
investment. This doesn't only mean designing and manufacturing chips but also 
owning those chips and the physical infrastructures on which they run—namely, data 
centers and their hardware components. Having access to these resources can 
present a competitive edge. This is not a shift per se but the opening of a new front 
in the AI race. Physical constraints apply—think power and water. 
↳ The implications 
New types of businesses and business models will emerge. Companies may shift 
focus—Yandex (popularly known in the past as “Russia’s Google”) provides an 
insightful example at the intersection of AI and the global geopolitical situation. VC 
firms focusing on AI, such as Andreessen Horowitz, are changing the investment 
dynamics in AI companies, using hardware to attract startups. Big tech and data 
center owners/operators are hungry for power, particularly clean power. The 
----------------Page (270) Break----------------
availability of clean energy and water will become a competitive advantage for 
regions and countries looking to attract that type of investment.

 The G20 talked CBDCs 
↳ Why does it matter? 
----------------Page (271) Break----------------
115 countries around the world are actively working on Central Bank Digital Currency

banking and financial services providers, and shift the use of currencies globally. 
Cross-border payment systems based on CBDCs can further facilitate the use of 
local currencies in global trade. 
↳ The implications

benefits   to emerging nations, as the African examples illustrate. Back to the 
sanctions topic, those can erode trust in the dollar-based system, as Secretary Yellen 
hinted. Stay tuned and don't miss the bandwagon; a lot is likely to happen in the 
digital money realm, from both businesses and governments.

 China talked ‘reforms’ 
↳ Why does it matter? 
China is the world's second-largest economy. Growth slowed in Q2 2024 and 
geopolitical competition is at a high point. The most used words in the communiqué 
of the CPC Central Committee plenum were: reform, economy and market. Themes 
on the rise include security, technology, risk, productivity and quality. What do they 
mean? The future of the planet is closely tied to China and its relationship with the 
US. 
----------------Page (273) Break----------------
↳ The implications

leaders there and make sense of what they mean by ‘reform’, the prospects for the 
economy and global relations. US-China connections are becoming more scarce, 
which can lead to miscalculations and increase global risk. ‘Reading’ China is not for 
amateurs, but most of the emerging world (and others) lacks the necessary 
capabilities—who speaks and reads Chinese well and is acquainted with the Chinese 
reality in your country? Fasten your seat belts.

 The EU’s regulation on AI fuels the conversation about risks 
versus innovation 
↳ Why does it matter? 
AI is the hottest technology today, attracting significant   investment and attention, 
driving innovation, and creating value at warp speed. AI is hungry for energy and 
data. Having access to data at a low cost is a competitive advantage for AI 
companies. What data can they use? Countries are taking different paths to regulate 
AI, and that directly affects the business of AI companies and big tech, the lives of all 
of us, and national economies. 
----------------Page (274) Break----------------
↳ The implications 
It is very hard to regulate something that is poorly understood and is evolving fast. 
Economies are interconnected, and if a country curbs the moves of AI and digital 
tech companies, they may decide to move operations elsewhere, impacting 
innovation capacity and the economy. The whole discussion is about “Safeguarding 
citizens versus Fostering innovation.” Global coordination is key in this game, and 
even the US and China are collaborating on the matter. The future of AI regulation 
will depend a lot on the US election. Stay tuned. 
↳ Read more here 

 A hiccup in space exploration 
↳ Why does it matter? 
Space is a major frontier for science and innovation, and space exploration is a 
costly and risky business. NASA’s decision to cancel the rover that would search for 
water on the Moon has the potential to affect commercial endeavors. It also sends 
----------------Page (275) Break----------------
signals about the capacity of the US to continue investing to sustain its technology 
leadership. China has recently recovered samples from the dark side of the Moon, 
and other nations are ramping up space activities. NASA’s announcement comes as 
new discoveries on Mars point to the past existence of water on the planet. 
↳ The implications 
This is part of a larger play in the US. Due to the debt ceiling deal the administration 
struck with Congress, the National Science Foundation and other agencies are also 
struggling with their budgets. For global leadership, knowledge matters, and science 
and technology matter. On the other hand, this is a clear reminder that the future of 
private space exploration depends on government money, which trickles down from 
NASA contracts to the private sector. The new space economy still needs a push to 
take off. Hope? NASA is offering the rover to other space agencies, with 
manifestations of interest due on Aug 1.
